# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# gRPC Error Status Propagation Across Go Services

## Your Task

Compare how gRPC error status codes are created and propagated in kubernetes/kubernetes vs grafana/grafana vs etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that create gRPC Status errors with codes (codes.NotFound, codes.Internal, etc.) and the files that translate gRPC errors to HTTP responses.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

68-assistanttext-
I've successfully analyzed gRPC error status propagation across the three repositories and created a comprehensive answer. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Key Findings

**Kubernetes/kubernetes:**
- Creates gRPC errors directly in utility functions and service mocks
- Uses `staging/src/k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/cri/streaming/errors.go:WriteError()` as the central translation point
- Manually maps gRPC codes to HTTP status codes via switch statement
- Example: `codes.ResourceExhausted` → `http.StatusTooManyRequests`

**Grafana/grafana:**
- Creates errors throughout interceptors and service methods (auth, RBAC, authz)
- Uses `pkg/storage/unified/resource/errors.go:AsErrorResult()` for conversion
- Leverages grpc-gateway v2's `runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode()` for standard code mapping
- Sets up custom error handlers with `runtime.WithErrorHandler()` in gateway configuration

**etcd-io/etcd:**
- Pre-defines all gRPC errors as package variables in `api/v3rpc/rpctypes/error.go`
- Uses `server/etcdserver/api/v3rpc/util.go:togRPCError()` to map internal errors to gRPC status errors
- Relies on grpc-gateway's generated handlers and automatic gRPC-to-HTTP conversion
- Maintains comprehensive error mapping for domain-specific errors (member, auth, lease, etc.)

The complete analysis with file paths, symbols, error chains, and detailed explanations has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`.

**Kubernetes**: Manual switch-case mapping in `WriteError()`\\n   - **Grafana**: Uses grpc-gateway's built-in `runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode()` utility\\n   - **etcd**: Maps internal errors to pre-defined gRPC errors, then relies on grpc-gateway for HTTP conversion\\n\\n3. **HTTP Status Code Mapping:**\\n   - **Kubernetes**: Explicit mapping in the `WriteError()` function\\n   - **Grafana**: Leverages grpc-gateway's standard gRPC-to-HTTP code mapping\\n   - **etcd**: Relies entirely on grpc-gateway's automatic conversion based on gRPC status codes\\n\\n4. **Gateway Integration:**\\n   - Maintains a `toGRPCErrorMap` (lines 35-96) that maps internal error types to gRPC status errors\\n  - For unmapped errors, returns `status.Error(codes.Unknown, err.Error())`\\n  - Preserves context-based errors (Canceled, DeadlineExceeded) for special handling\\n\\n**Error Propagation to HTTP:**\\n- `api/etcdserverpb/gw/rpc.pb.gw.go`, `server/etcdserver/api/v3election/v3electionpb/gw/v3election.pb.gw.go`, `server/etcdserver/api/v3lock/v3lockpb/gw/v3lock.pb.gw.go`: Generated gRPC-gateway code that:\\n  - Automatically translates gRPC errors to HTTP responses\\n  - Uses marshaler to decode requests (lines 660-661, etc.)\\n  - Returns `status.Errorf(codes.InvalidArgument, ...)` for malformed requests\\n  - The gRPC-gateway runtime handles conversion of gRPC codes to HTTP status codes\\n\\n- `server/embed/serve.go`: Registers the gateway with custom error handlers for HTTP-to-gRPC conversion (lines 322-324)\\n\\n### Key Differences in Approaches\\n\\n1. **Error Definition:**\\n   - **Kubernetes**: Defines errors inline in utility functions\\n   - **Grafana**: Creates errors in interceptors and service methods\\n   - **etcd**: Pre-defines all errors as package-level variables for reuse\\n\\n2. **Error Translation Strategy:**\\n   - **Kubernetes**: Manual switch-case mapping in `WriteError()`\\n   - **Grafana**: Uses grpc-gateway's built-in `runtime.HTTPStatusFromCode()` utility\\n   - **etcd**: Maps internal errors to pre-defined gRPC errors, then relies on grpc-gateway for HTTP conversion\\n\\n3. **HTTP Status Code Mapping:**\\n   - **Kubernetes**: Explicit mapping in the `WriteError()` function\\n   - **Grafana**: Leverages grpc-gateway's standard gRPC-to-HTTP code mapping\\n   - **etcd**: Relies entirely on grpc-gateway's automatic conversion based on gRPC status codes\\n\\n4. **Gateway Integration:**\\n   - **Kubernetes**: No gRPC-gateway; direct HTTP-to-gRPC conversion in streaming server\\n   - **Grafana**: Uses grpc-gateway v2 with custom error handlers and middleware\\n   - **etcd**: Uses grpc-gateway for REST API translation with generated handlers\\n\\nThe common pattern across all three is the use of Google's gRPC status package to define errors with specific codes, which then get translated to HTTP status codes either manually or through gRPC-gateway's runtime utilities.\"\n}\n",
